- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retry safety is a precondition, not a policy, the doctrine orders the work so the key exists before the retry, because a retry policy added to unkeyed writes converts transient failures into permanent duplicates

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's evidence bullets stand while the doctrine's observability doctrine is implicit in its design, explicit results make failure paths enumerable in code, branded types make identifier flows traceable in signatures, boundary parsing concentrates rejection events at instrumentable edges, and the skimmable-boundary expectation makes the risky seam findable by a reader, observability by construction rather than by tooling
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine's defenses all externalize what exception-based code hides, an error union is a complete catalog of what a function admits can go wrong, so the code base itself becomes the observability layer's schema
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the observability hole is the throw side, invariant violations still travel as exceptions by design, and services that instrument only their result paths lose exactly the failures that indicate programmer bugs, the split needing both channels watched

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's latency packet stands beside the doctrine's actual performance content, deadline propagation as the performance backstop, every boundary bounded by AbortSignal timeouts so slow dependencies fail fast instead of accumulating, and project-reference partitions as build performance, the doctrine treating runtime speed as someone else's subject and time bounds as reliability
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine optimizes for predictability over throughput, a bounded slow call is a handled failure while an unbounded fast call is a latent outage, deadlines converting performance variance into typed, testable failure paths
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: deadline-free chains fail collectively, one slow provider stalls the handler, the queue backs up, and the outage arrives everywhere at once, the doctrine's timeout drift naming exactly this accumulation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the doctrine's performance-adjacent content, the seed's measurement packet remains the reporting format
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the bounded-time reading, deadlines as reliability, partitions as build speed, throughput deliberately unclaimed
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that deadline propagation makes latency budgets compositional, a handler with a 2-second budget can allocate portions to each downstream call through the signal chain, performance management becoming an architectural property of the call graph rather than a tuning activity, budget arithmetic replacing profiling for the first-order decisions

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's distributed-execution paragraphs stand while the doctrine's own scale limits go unnamed, the patterns govern one service's boundaries, cross-service consistency, distributed transactions, and saga orchestration exceed the idempotency pattern's single-write scope, the persistence contract covers format evolution, not sharding or migration at volume, and the project-reference pattern is the doctrine's only concession to codebase scale
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine's unit is the service boundary, its defenses compose within one deployable and stop where coordination between deployables begins, distributed correctness needing machinery, outboxes, sagas, consensus, the doctrine never claims
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the characteristic overreach is stretching pattern eight into distributed transactions, a dedup key protects one write, coordinating writes across services with keys alone reinvents two-phase commit badly, the pattern's scope ending at the database the key lives in
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale limits of the doctrine, corpus-execution splitting stays in the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the three boundaries, single-service scope, format-not-volume persistence, and the compiler-support concession
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the doctrine scales down better than up, every pattern applies to a single-file CLI, parse argv, brand the paths, result the failures, bound the runtime, while the upward direction needs new doctrine entirely, boundary discipline being scale-invariant toward smallness because seams exist at every size
